title="Al-Shu'ala">Al-Shu'ala</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Mahmudiyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Mahmudiyah">Al-Mahmudiyah</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Bab_Al-Moatham" title="Bab Al-Moatham">Bab Al-Moatham</a>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Baiyaa" title="Baiyaa">Al-Baya'</a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Za%27franiya" title="Al-Za'franiya">Al-Za'franiya</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayy_Ur" title="Hayy Ur">Hayy Ur</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Sha%27ab,_Baghdad" title="Sha'ab, Baghdad">Sha'ab</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Jamia" title="Jamia">Hayy Al-Jami'a</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Adel" title="Al-Adel">Al-Adel</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al_Khadhraa" title="Al Khadhraa">Al Khadhraa</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayy_Al-Jihad" class="mw-redirect" title="Hayy Al-Jihad">Hayy Al-Jihad</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayy_Al-A%27amel" title="Hayy Al-A'amel">Hayy Al-A'amel</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayy_Aoor" title="Hayy Aoor">Hayy Aoor</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Hurriya" title="Al-Hurriya">Al-Hurriya</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayy_Al-Shurtta" title="Hayy Al-Shurtta">Hayy Al-Shurtta</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Yarmouk,_Baghdad" title="Yarmouk, Baghdad">Yarmouk</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Jesr_Diyala" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesr Diyala">Jesr Diyala</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Abu_Disher" title="Abu Disher">Abu Disher</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Raghiba_Khatoun" title="Raghiba Khatoun">Raghiba Khatoun</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Arab_Jibor" title="Arab Jibor">Arab Jibor</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Fathel" title="Al-Fathel">Al-Fathel</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Ubedy" title="Al-Ubedy">Al-Ubedy</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Washash" title="Al-Washash">Al-Washash</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Wazireya" title="Al-Wazireya">Al-Wazireya</a></li>/n</ul>/n</div>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>Baghdad's population was estimated at 7.22 million in 2015. The city historically had a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> population, by the early 21st century around 82% of the city's population were <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Iraq" title="Shia Islam in Iraq">Iraqi Shia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> At the beginning of the 21st century, some 1.5 million people migrated to Baghdad, most of them Shiites and a few Sunnis.</p>/n<p>As early as 2003, about 20 percent of the population of the city was the result of mixed marriages between Shi'ites and Sunnis: they are often referred to as "Sushis".<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/Sectarian_violence_in_Iraq_(2006%E2%80%9307)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sectarian violence in Iraq (2006–07)">ethnic cleansing campaigns</a> by Sunni and then Shia militia groups during the U.S. occupation of Iraq the city's population became overwhelmingly Shia and despite the government's promise to resettle Sunnis displaced by the violence, little has been done to bring this about. The <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Iraqi Civil War (2014–present)">Iraqi Civil War following ISIS' invasion</a> in 2014 caused hundreds of thousands of Iraqi internally displaced people to flee to the city. The city currently has Shia, Sunni, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrian Christian">Assyrian Christian</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint Inline-Template" style="vertical-align:text-top;white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dispenser.info.tm/~dispenser/cgi-bin/dab_solver.py?page=Baghdad&amp;editintro=Template:Disambiguation_needed/editintro&amp;client=Template:Dn"><span title="Link needs disambiguation. (June 2017)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and mixed neighborhoods but is the world's second largest Shia city after <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">/n<tr>/n<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>/n<td class="mbox-text">/n<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(December 2009)</i></small></div>/n</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>Baghdad accounts for 22.2 per cent of Iraq's population and 40 per cent of the country's gross domestic product (PPP). <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Airways" title="Iraqi Airways">Iraqi Airways</a>, the national airline of Iraq, has its headquarters on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_International_Airport" title="Baghdad International Airport">Baghdad International Airport</a> in Baghdad.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al-Naser_Airlines" title="Al-Naser Airlines">Al-Naser Airlines</a> has its head office in <a href="/wiki/Karrada" title="Karrada">Karrada</a>, Baghdad.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reconstruction_efforts">Reconstruction efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Reconstruction efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Investment_in_post-invasion_Iraq" title="Investment in post-invasion Iraq">Investment in post-invasion Iraq</a></div>/n<p>Most <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Reconstruction of Iraq">Iraqi reconstruction</a> efforts have been devoted to the restoration and repair of badly damaged urban infrastructure. More visible efforts at reconstruction through private development, like architect and urban designer <a href="/wiki/Hisham_N._Ashkouri" title="Hisham N. Ashkouri">Hisham N. Ashkouri</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_of_Iraq#The_Proposed_Baghdad_Baghdad_is_mizz_Renaissance_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Reconstruction of Iraq">Baghdad Renaissance Plan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sindbad_Hotel_Complex_and_Conference_Center" title="Sindbad Hotel Complex and Conference Center">Sindbad Hotel Complex and Conference Center</a> have also been made. <sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> A plan was proposed by a Government agency to rebuild a tourist island in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-83">[82]</a></sup> In late 2009, a construction plan was proposed to rebuild the heart of Baghdad, but the plan was never realized because corruption was involved in it.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2-84">[83]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The Baghdad Eye, a 198&#160;m (650&#160;ft) tall <a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a>, was proposed for Baghdad in August 2008. At that time, three possible locations had been identified, but no estimates of cost or completion date were given.<sup id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com.2Fid.2F26425911_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com.2Fid.2F26425911-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> In October 2008, it was reported that Al-Zawraa Park was expected to be the site,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> and a 55&#160;m (180&#160;ft) wheel was installed there in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Iraq's Tourism Board is also seeking investors to develop a "romantic" island on the River Tigris in Baghdad that was once a popular honeymoon spot for newlywed Iraqis. The project would include a six-star hotel, spa, an 18-hole golf course and a country club. In addition, the go-ahead has been given to build numerous architecturally unique skyscrapers along the Tigris that would develop the city's financial centre in Kadhehemiah.<sup id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com.2Fid.2F26425911_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com.2Fid.2F26425911-85">[84]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In October 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Metro" title="Baghdad Metro">Baghdad Metro</a> resumed service. It connects the center to the southern neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Dora,_Baghdad" title="Dora, Baghdad">Dora</a>. In May 2010, a new residential and commercial project nicknamed <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad_Gate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baghdad Gate (page does not exist)">Baghdad Gate</a> was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> This project not only addresses the urgent need for new residential units in Baghdad but also acts as a real symbol of progress in the war torn city, as Baghdad has not seen projects of this scale for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retails">Retails</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Retails">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<ul>/n<li>Baghdad | Baghdad Mall (4 floors) + Baghdad Rayhan Hotel by Rotana + offices (30 floors) (105 metres) + offices (7 floors)</li>/n</ul>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<ul>/n<li>Baghdad | Taji | 60,000 seats Stadium.</li>/n</ul>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<ul>/n<li>Baghdad | Bismayah New City | 100,000 housing units.</li>/n<li>Baghdad | Zuhour | 5400 units (100 apartments)</li>/n<li>Baghdad | Ibn Firnas Residential Project | 2016 housing Units</li>/n<li>Baghdad | Al Ayadi Residential Project | 1335 housing Units</li>/n<li>Baghdad | Riyadh Apartments | 8 floors</li>/n</ul>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">/n<tr>/n<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>/n<td class="mbox-text">/n<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small></div>/n</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mustansiriya_Madrasah" title="Mustansiriya Madrasah">Mustansiriya Madrasah</a> was established in 1227 by the Abbasid Caliph al-Mustansir. The name was changed to <a href="/wiki/Al-Mustansiriya_University" title="Al-Mustansiriya University">Al-Mustansiriya University</a> in 1963. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Baghdad" title="University of Baghdad">University of Baghdad</a> is the largest university in Iraq and the second largest in the Arab world.</p>/n<p>Prior to the Gulf War multiple <a href="/wiki/International_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="International schools">international schools</a> operated in Baghdad, including:</p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_fran%C3%A7aise_de_Bagdad&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="École française de Bagdad (page does not exist)">École française de Bagdad</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></li>/n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deutsche_Schule_Bagdad&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Deutsche Schule Bagdad (page does not exist)">Deutsche Schule Bagdad</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></li>/n<li>Baghdad Japanese School (バグダッド日本人学校), a <a href="/wiki/Nihonjin_gakko" class="mw-redirect" title="Nihonjin gakko">nihonjin gakko</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></li>/n</ul>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Mustansiriya_University" title="Al-Mustansiriya University">Al-Mustansiriya University</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Iraqi_University" title="Iraqi University">Iraqi University</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Nahrain_University" title="Nahrain University">Nahrain University</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Baghdad" title="University of Baghdad">University of Baghdad</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Technology,_Iraq" title="University of Technology, Iraq">University of Technology, Iraq</a></li>/n</ul>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Arabic" title="Baghdad Arabic">Baghdad Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iraq" title="Culture of Iraq">Culture of Iraq</a></div>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg/220px-Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg/330px-Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg/440px-Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="433" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_National_Orchestra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra">Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra</a>, officially founded in 1959, performing a concert in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> in July 2007.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Baghdad has always played a significant role in the broader <a href="/wiki/Arab_culture" title="Arab culture">Arab cultural sphere</a>, contributing several significant writers, musicians and visual artists. Famous <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> poets and singers such as <a href="/wiki/Nizar_Qabbani" title="Nizar Qabbani">Nizar Qabbani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umm_Kulthum" title="Umm Kulthum">Umm Kulthum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fairuz" title="Fairuz">Fairuz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salah_Al-Hamdani" title="Salah Al-Hamdani">Salah Al-Hamdani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilham_al-Madfai" title="Ilham al-Madfai">Ilham al-Madfai</a> and others have performed for the city.</p>/n<p>The dialect of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Arabic" title="Baghdad Arabic">Arabic spoken in Baghdad</a> today differs from that of other large urban centres in Iraq, having features more characteristic of nomadic Arabic dialects (Verseegh, <i>The Arabic Language</i>). It is possible that this was caused by the repopulating of the city with rural residents after the multiple sacks of the late <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.</p>/n<p>For poetry written about Baghdad, see <a href="/wiki/Reuven_Snir" title="Reuven Snir">Reuven Snir</a> (ed.), <i>Baghdad: The City in Verse</i> (Harvard, 2013)<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.hup.harvard.edu/features/baghdad/">[3]</a></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions">Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg/220px-Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg/330px-Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg/440px-Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="419" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iraq-National_unity_ballet2_600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nTwo <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a> dancers of the Iraqi National Ballet (which is based in Baghdad) performing a ballet show in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> in 2007.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/220px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/330px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/440px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="1960" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nMany events are hosted at the Baghdad Convention Center</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Some of the important cultural institutions in the city include:</p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra">Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra</a> – Rehearsals and performances were briefly interrupted during the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Second Gulf War</a>, but have since returned to normal</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/National_Theater_(Iraq)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Theater (Iraq)">National Theater</a> – The theatre was looted during the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, but efforts are underway to restore the theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></li>/n</ul>/n<p>The live theatre scene received a boost during the 1990s, when UN <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">sanctions</a> limited the import of foreign films. As many as 30 movie theatres were reported to have been converted to live stages, producing a wide range of <a href="/wiki/Comedy" title="Comedy">comedies</a> and dramatic productions.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Institutions offering cultural education in Baghdad include <a href="/wiki/The_Music_and_Ballet_School_of_Baghdad" title="The Music and Ballet School of Baghdad">The Music and Ballet School of Baghdad</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Institute_of_Fine_Arts_Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Institute of Fine Arts Baghdad (page does not exist)">Institute of Fine Arts Baghdad</a>. Baghdad is also home to a number of museums which housed <a href="/wiki/Artifact_(archaeology)" title="Artifact (archaeology)">artifacts</a> and relics of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient civilization">ancient civilization</a>; many of these were stolen, and the museums looted, during the widespread chaos immediately after United States forces entered the city.</p>/n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%9311)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Iraq (2003–11)">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/AFN_Iraq" title="AFN Iraq">AFN Iraq</a> ("Freedom Radio") broadcast news and entertainment within Baghdad, among other locations. There is also a private radio station called "Dijlah" (named after the Arabic word for the Tigris River) that was created in 2004 as Iraq's first independent talk radio station. Radio Dijlah offices, in the <a href="/wiki/Jamia" title="Jamia">Jamia</a> neighborhood of Baghdad, have been attacked on several occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>Baghdad is home to some of the most successful <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football (soccer)</a> teams in Iraq, the biggest being <a href="/wiki/Al-Shorta_SC" title="Al-Shorta SC">Al-Shorta</a> (Police), <a href="/wiki/Al-Quwa_Al-Jawiya" title="Al-Quwa Al-Jawiya">Al-Quwa Al-Jawiya</a> (Airforce club), <a href="/wiki/Al-Zawra%27a_SC" title="Al-Zawra'a SC">Al-Zawra'a</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Talaba_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Talaba SC">Talaba</a> (Students). The largest stadium in Baghdad is <a href="/wiki/Al-Shaab_Stadium" title="Al-Shaab Stadium">Al-Shaab Stadium</a>, which was opened in 1966. Another, but much larger stadium, is still in the opening stages of construction.</p>/n<p>The city has also had a strong tradition of <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> ever since <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, known to Baghdadis simply as 'Races'. There are reports of pressures by the Islamists to stop this tradition due to the associated gambling.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_streets">Major streets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Iraq" title="List of places in Iraq">List of places in Iraq</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Firdos_Square" title="Firdos Square">Firdos Square</a> - is a public open space in Baghdad and the location of two of the best-known hotels, the Palestine Hotel and the Sheraton Ishtar, which are both also the tallest buildings in Baghdad. The square was the site of the statue of Saddam Hussein that was pulled down by U.S. coalition forces in a widely televised event during the 2003 invasion of Iraq.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Imposing_Law" title="Operation Imposing Law">Operation Imposing Law</a> Baghdad Security Plan</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Anti-Zionist_League_in_Iraq" title="Anti-Zionist League in Iraq">Anti-Zionist League in Iraq</a> - founded in Baghdad in 1945</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Baghdad_(1917)" title="Fall of Baghdad (1917)">Fall of Baghdad</a> 1917</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(946)" title="Battle of Baghdad (946)">Battle of Baghdad</a> 946</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(2003)" title="Battle of Baghdad (2003)">Battle of Baghdad 2003</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(812%E2%80%93813)" title="Siege of Baghdad (812–813)">Siege of Baghdad 812-3</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1157)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1157)">Siege of Baghdad 1157</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">Siege of Baghdad 1258</a></li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1733)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1733)">Siege of Baghdad 1733</a></li>/n</ul>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baghdad&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">/n<div class="mw-references-wrap">/n<ol class="references">/n<li id="cite_note-population-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-population_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-population_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Estimates of total population differ substantially. The <a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Britannica" class="mw-redirect" title="Encyclopedia Britannica">Encyclopedia Britannica</a> gives the city 2001-2006 population of 4,950,000;<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s).
